<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block"><br>
</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The Registrant is the depositor under the trust agreements for its various SATURNS Units listed on the New York Stock Exchange.&#160;&#160;The Units do not represent obligations of or interests in the Depositor. Pursuant to staff administrative positions established in various no-action letters, see e.g. Corporate Asset Backed Corporation (available August 9, 1995), the Registrant is not required to respond to various items of Form 10-K. Such items are designated herein as &#8220;Not applicable.&#8221;&#160;&#160;Distribution reports detailing receipts and distributions by each trust are filed shortly after each distribution date on Form 8-K in lieu of reports on Form 10-Q.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The underlying security issuer or guarantor, as applicable, of the securities held by each of the trusts is subject to the informational requirements of the Exchange Act.&#160;&#160;The underlying security issuer or guarantor, as applicable, currently files reports, proxy statements and other information with the SEC.&#160;&#160;For information regarding such underlying security issuer or guarantor, you should refer to such reports.&#160;&#160;These periodic, current and other reports and other information can be inspected and copied at the public reference facilities maintained by the SEC at Room 1024, 100 F Street, N.E., Washington, D.C. 20549. Copies of those materials can be obtained by making a written request to the SEC, Public Reference Section, 100 F Street, N.E., Washington, D.C. 20549, at prescribed rates. The SEC also maintains a website on the internet at http://www.sec.gov at which users can view and download copies of reports, proxy, information statements and other information filed electronically.&#160;&#160;In addition, those reports and other information may also be obtained from the underlying security issuer by making a request to the underlying security issuer.&#160;&#160;The trust, the trustee, the Registrant, and their affiliates have not verified, have not undertaken to verify, and will not verify, the content of any such reports or information. The name and the central index key (CIK) for each underlying security issuer or guarantor is set forth below:</font></div>

<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 8pt">&#160; </font></div>
</div>
</div>

<br>
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block"><br>
</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 396pt"></font>EXHIBIT B</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">False Claims Act</font></font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">With respect to paragraph 7 of this certificate, the U.S. Government is conducting a civil investigation under the False Claims Act into whether originators, depositors, servicers, or trustees of residential mortgage-backed securities (&#8220;<font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">RMBS</font>&#8221;) trusts submitted false claims for payment by&#160; government purchasers of RMBS by (1) concealing that the trusts lacked collateral documents necessary to foreclose; (2) charging RMBS trusts for fraudulent loan processing services, including the preparation of fraudulent mortgage assignments; and (3) failing to ensure that the RMBS trusts paid necessary real estate mortgage investment conduit (&#8220;<font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">REMIC</font>&#8221;) taxes.&#160; Certain states may be conducting similar investigations.&#160; The investigation may involve RMBS trusts in which current or former Bank of America affiliates, including BAC Home Loans Servicing LP, Bank of America Mortgage Securities, Inc., Countrywide Financial Corporation, and Bank of America, N.A. as successor by merger to LaSalle Bank, served as originator, depositor, servicer, or trustee.&#160; The U.S. government&#8217;s investigation is also considering whether participants in RMBS trusts defrauded federal mortgage insurers, including the Federal Housing Administration and the Department of Housing and Urban Development by submitting claims for loan guarantee payments on loans for which the trusts lacked collateral documents necessary to foreclose.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Investigations under the federal and most state False Claims Acts may be initiated by the applicable government investigative body or by a <font style="FONT-STYLE: italic; DISPLAY: inline">qui tam </font>relator&#8217;s filing of a False Claims Act complaint under court seal.&#160; If a <font style="FONT-STYLE: italic; DISPLAY: inline">qui tam </font>relator&#8217;s complaint remained under seal, applicable law would restrict our ability to disclose such a fact.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Ocala</font></font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Bank of America, National Association is a named party in litigation involving Ocala Funding, LLP.&#160;&#160;Information about this litigation is publicly disclosed in Bank of America Corporation&#8217;s Form 10-K and Form 10-Q filings.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Fifth Third v. Concord Capital Management et al.</font></font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Bank of America, National Association (&#8220;<font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Bank of America</font>&#8221;) was named as a co-defendant in a suit filed in September 2010 by Concord Capital Management LLC and affiliated parties (collectively, &#8220;<font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Concord</font>&#8221;) in the New York State Supreme Court against Bank of America (as successor by merger to LaSalle Bank National Association), Fifth Third Bank (&#8220;<font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Fifth Third</font>&#8221;) and other parties. The suit alleged gross negligence and breach of contract by Bank of America, acting as collateral agent, servicer and, until the transfer of such role to Wilmington Trust Company in February 2009, the trustee, in connection with a life insurance premium-financing loan facility known as &#8220;Ultra&#8221;, established by Concord and financed by Fifth Third.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">In November 2011, Fifth Third filed an amended complaint in Illinois State Court naming Concord, Bank of America and certain other parties, as defendants. Fifth Third&#8217;s lawsuit alleges breach of contract and gross negligence by Bank of America based on assertions about Bank of America&#8217;s duties substantially similar to those previously made by Concord in New York State Court.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block"><br>
</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Bank of America&#8217;s motion to dismiss against Concord was granted on December 5, 2011. The Fifth Third lawsuit is ongoing.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Nightingale Properties, LLC et al. vs. Bank of America, N.A., et al.</font></font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Bank of America was named as a co-defendant with CW Capital Asset Management LLC (&#8220;<font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">CWC</font>&#8221;) in suits filed in Tennessee State Court (in February 2011) New York State Court (in August 2011) and Federal District Court for the Southern District of New York (in December 2011) by the Nightingale Group, LLC and related parties (collectively, &#8220;<font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Nightingale</font>&#8221;). Each of the actions arose as a consequence of the default of four commercial loans in the LB-UBS Commercial Mortgage Trust, 2008-C1, and the filing by CWC on behalf of Bank of America of a collection suit in Tennessee against Nightingale and its owners/guarantors, which resulted in a receivership.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The Tennessee and New York State complaints allege libel by CWC, as servicer, purportedly acting as agent of Bank of America, as trustee with respect to the LB-UBS Trust, arising from the publication by CWC of certain statements relating to the guarantee given by Nightingale in support of payment on the four commercial loans in the LB-UBS Trust. The Federal District Court complaint alleges breach of contract, intentional or negligent interference with prospective economic advantage, fraud, promissory estoppel and a RICO claim against CWC and Bank of America.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<br>
<div id="PGBRK" style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">

<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; FONT-SIZE: 8pt">&#160; </font></div>
